on LDL particle size as a risk factor for CVD has not been examined. We compared, in the same subjects, the impact of a dietary portfolio of cholesterol-lowering foods and a statin on LDL size electrophoretic characteristics. Thirty-four hyperlipidaemic subjects completed three 1-month treatments as outpatients in random order: a very-low saturated fat diet (control); the same diet with 20\u00a0mg lovastatin; a dietary portfolio high in plant sterols (1\u00a0g/4200\u00a0kJ), soya proteins (21\u00b74\u00a0g/4200\u00a0kJ), soluble fibres (9\u00b78\u00a0g/4200\u00a0kJ) and almonds (14\u00a0g/4200\u00a0kJ). LDL electrophoretic characteristics were measured by non-denaturing polyacrylamide gradient gel electrophoresis of fasting plasma at 0, 2 and 4 weeks of each treatment. The reductions in plasma LDL-cholesterol levels with the dietary portfolio and with statins were comparable and were largely attributable to reductions in the estimated concentration of cholesterol within the smallest subclass of LDL (portfolio \u2212\u00a00\u00b769\u00a0(<jats:sc>se</jats:sc> 0\u00b710) mmol/l, statin \u2212\u00a00\u00b799 (<jats:sc>se</jats:sc> 0\u00b710) mmol/l). These were significantly greater (<jats:italic>P</jats:italic>\u00a0&lt;\u00a00\u00b701) than changes observed after the control diet (\u00a0\u2212\u00a00\u00b717 (<jats:sc>se</jats:sc> 0\u00b708) mmol/l). Finally, baseline C-reactive protein levels were a significant predictor of the LDL size responsiveness to the dietary portfolio but not to the other treatments. The dietary portfolio, like the statin treatment, had only minor effects on several features of the LDL size phenotype, but the pronounced reduction in cholesterol levels within the small LDL fraction may provide additional cardiovascular benefit over the traditional low-fat diet of National Cholesterol Education Program Step II.</jats:p>", "DOI": "10.1017/s0007114507781461", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2007, 7, 30]], "date-time": "2007-07-30T13:37:34Z", "timestamp": 1185802654000}, "page": "1229-1236", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 19, "title": ["Comparison of a dietary portfolio diet of cholesterol-lowering foods and a statin on LDL particle size phenotype in hypercholesterolaemic participants"], "prefix": "10.1017", "volume": "98", "author": [{"given": "Iris", "family": "Gigleux", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "David J. "unspecified"}], "content-domain": {"domain": [], "crossmark-restriction": false}, "short-container-title": ["Br J Nutr"], "published-print": {"date-parts": [[2011, 11, 14]]}, "abstract": "<jats:p>The well-documented lipid-lowering effects of fibre may be related to its viscosity, a phenomenon that has been understudied, especially when fibre is given against the background of a typical North American (NA) diet. In this three-arm experiment, we compared the lipid-lowering effect of low-viscosity wheat bran (WB), medium-viscosity psyllium (PSY) and a high-viscosity viscous fibre blend (VFB), as part of a fibre intervention aimed at increasing fibre intake to recommended levels within the context of a NA diet in apparently healthy individuals. Using a randomised cross-over design, twenty-three participants (twelve males and eleven females; age 35 (<jats:sc>sd</jats:sc> 12) years; LDL-cholesterol (C) 2\u00b79 (<jats:sc>sem</jats:sc> 0\u00b76) mmol/l) consuming a typical NA diet received a standard, fibre-enriched cereal, where approximately one-third of the fibre was either a low-viscosity (570 centipoise (cP)) WB, medium-viscosity (14\u00a0300\u00a0cP) PSY or a high-viscosity (136\u00a0300\u00a0cP) novel VFB, for 3 weeks separated by washout periods of \u2265\u00a02 weeks. There were no differences among the treatments in the amount of food consumed, total dietary fibre intake, reported physical activity and body weight. Final intake of the WB, PSY and VFB was 10\u00b78, 9\u00b70 and 5\u00b71\u00a0g, respectively. Reduction in LDL-C was greater with the VFB compared with the medium-viscosity PSY (\u00a0\u2212\u00a012\u00b76 (<jats:sc>sem</jats:sc> 3\u00b75) %, <jats:italic>P</jats:italic>\u00a0=\u00a00\u00b7002) and low-viscosity WB (\u00a0\u2212\u00a014\u00b76 (<jats:sc>sem</jats:sc> 4\u00b72)\u00a0%, <jats:italic>P</jats:italic>\u00a0=\u00a00\u00b7003). The magnitude of LDL-C reduction showed a positive association with fibre apparent viscosity (<jats:italic>r</jats:italic> \u2212\u00a00\u00b741, <jats:italic>P</jats:italic>\u00a0=\u00a00\u00b7001). Despite the smaller quantity consumed, the high-viscosity fibre lowered LDL-C to a greater extent than lower-viscosity fibres. These data support the inclusion of high-viscosity fibre in the diet to reduce plasma lipids among apparently healthy individuals consuming a typical NA diet.</jats:p>", "DOI": "10.1017/s0007114511001711", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2011, 5, 31]], "date-time": "2011-05-31T12:46:20Z", "timestamp": 1306845980000}, "page": "1349-1352", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 48, "title": ["Viscosity rather than quantity of dietary fibre predicts cholesterol-lowering effect in healthy individuals"], "prefix": "10.1017", "volume": "106", "author": [{"given": "Vladimir", "family": "Vuksan", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Alexandra L.", "family": "Jenkins", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Alexander L.", "family": "Rogovik", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Christopher D.", "family": "Fairgrieve", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Elena", "family": "Jovanovski", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Lawrence A.", "family": "Leiter", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}], "member": "56", "published-online": {"date-parts": [[2011, 5, 31]]}, "reference": [{"key": "S0007114511001711_ref8", "DOI": "10.1080/10408390500511862", "doi-asserted-by": "publisher"}, {"key": "S0007114511001711_ref7", "year": "2002", "volume-title": "Dietary Reference Intakes: Energy, Carbohydrate, Fiber, Fat, Fatty Acids, Cholesterol, Protein, and Amino Acids"}, {"key": "S0007114511001711_ref10", "DOI": "10.2337/diacare.25.9.1522", "doi-asserted-by": "publisher"}, {"key": "S0007114511001711_ref9", "volume": "67", "first-page": "61773", "year": "2002", "article-title": "Food labeling: health claims; soluble dietary fiber from certain foods and coronary heart disease.
